## a16z Podcast | Dealing with Corporate Dealmakers -- When to Talk to Corp Dev

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IeDirae6h1E](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IeDirae6h1E)

- Corporate development: A function within a company that focuses on inorganic growth opportunities, such as investing in or acquiring other companies.
- Misconceptions about corporate development: Startup founders often view engaging with corporate development teams as a waste of time due to the perception that these meetings are long and drawn out processes. However, the corporate development team is typically interested in understanding the strategic landscape of their industry and how it might impact their company's growth plans.
- Engaging with corporate development teams: Founders should approach these meetings with a clear understanding of what they want to get out of them and be prepared to share information about their own company and its potential for partnership or acquisition. It is also important to manage the process effectively by setting expectations early on and avoiding giving too much or too little information at once.
- Building relationships with corporate development teams: Founders should aim to build strong relationships with these teams by understanding their needs and interests, as well as being open to discussing potential opportunities for collaboration. This can help ensure that both parties are on the same page when it comes to future partnerships or acquisitions.
- Understanding the role of corporate development teams in different industries: In the enterprise space, corporate development teams often focus on M&A execution, while in the consumer space they may be more focused on building products and partnerships. Founders should be aware of these differences when engaging with these teams.
- Strategic investments versus financial investments: Corporate development teams may also make strategic investments in startups that align with their long-term growth plans. These investments can provide founders with valuable resources and connections, but they also come with certain risks and considerations.
- Negotiating term sheets: When negotiating a term sheet for an investment or acquisition, it is important for both parties to understand the process and be prepared to discuss key issues such as diligence, valuation, and governance. Founders should also be aware of the different types of agreements that may be involved in these transactions (e.g., letter of intent, definitive agreement, merger agreement).
- Understanding the acquisition process: The acquisition process can vary widely depending on the size and complexity of the companies involved. Founders should be prepared to work closely with their corporate development team throughout this process, as well as seek advice from legal and financial advisors when necessary.

## a16z Podcast | Tech Trends Changing Gaming

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tjj4ejADvRo](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tjj4ejADvRo)

    - Funding Landscape: The rise of crowdfunding has allowed developers to have more creative control and a direct relationship with their audience. This has led to an increase in independent game development, which has also changed the business side of the gaming industry.
  
- Discovery and Crowdfunding: Developers are finding it difficult to be discovered on traditional platforms like Steam. They're turning to crowdfunding and community building as a way to generate buzz for their games and build a following.
  
- Mobile and VR Gaming: The rise of mobile gaming has brought in new players who may not have been part of the gaming industry before. These new players are changing the landscape of gaming, and developers are trying to figure out how to adapt to this new audience. Virtual reality is also gaining popularity, and developers are experimenting with how to create immersive experiences for players.
  
- Narrative and Gameplay: Developers are exploring different ways to tell stories in games, and they're looking for ways to make their gameplay more engaging. They're also trying to find ways to create authentic choices for players that will make the game feel more personal.
  
- Modding and Community Building: Modders and community members are playing a bigger role in the development of games. Developers are working closely with these groups to get feedback on their games and to help them improve.

These are just some of the key points discussed during the podcast. The conversation was wide-ranging and covered many different aspects of the gaming industry, including funding, discovery, mobile gaming, VR gaming, narrative, gameplay, modding, and community building.

- He also discussed how Google's focus on cloud computing allows them to continuously improve their products without having to release major updates every year.
- Finally, Evans touched upon the growing trend of virtual reality and augmented reality technologies, suggesting that both companies will likely continue to invest in these areas as they become more mainstream.

## a16z Podcast | Finding and Hiring for (Expectations) Fit on Both Sides

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jGX62JGdabo](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jGX62JGdabo)

- Fit is a critical aspect of hiring in startups
- Cultural fit and role fit are two dimensions to evaluate candidates
- The process of hiring involves creating a 100 day plan for the candidate
- A good cultural fit can lead to a successful hire that aligns with company values and expectations
- Misalignment in motivation or expectation could lead to sudden issues post-hire
- The interview process should involve a realistic depiction of the company culture, role, and expectations
- A strong 100 day plan helps both parties understand each other's expectations and goals
- The hiring manager should be open to feedback from the candidate during the interview process
- It is essential to consider the candidate's motivation and passion for the role and company
- The hiring team should work together to ensure a consistent message and understanding of the company culture and values
- A good cultural fit can lead to higher employee retention rates
- The 100 day plan should be a living document that evolves with the candidate's progress in the role

## a16z Podcast | Which Bitcoin Players Matter?

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KEF_nQ-Lirw](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KEF_nQ-Lirw)

- Nathaniel Popper, author of "Digital Gold: Bitcoin and the Inside Story of Misfits Trying to Reinvent Money," discusses his book and insights from Argentina's Bitcoin scene.
- He describes an experiment happening in Argentina where people are trading peso for Bitcoin and vice versa.
- The use of Bitcoin in Argentina is interesting because it allows something that ordinary currency cannot do.
- Popper believes that the Argentinian experience offers valuable lessons that might be used elsewhere, particularly when it comes to technology protocols and infrastructure improvements.
- He mentions a "working-class coined money changer" who makes the whole thing work.
- Popper emphasizes the importance of ordinary people using Bitcoin in everyday transactions as a way to validate its usefulness.
- He also discusses the potential for alternative currencies and how they could be used in countries with hyperinflation or economic instability, like Venezuela and Zimbabwe.
- The author talks about the evolution of the Internet and compares it to Bitcoin's growth, highlighting similarities between both technologies.
- He believes that Bitcoin is ready for "primetime" but acknowledges that there are still improvements needed before it can become a significant part of larger economies.
- Popper also addresses the tension between decentralized and centralized players in the Bitcoin ecosystem, noting that many people don't trust centralized institutions like banks but rely on them anyway.
- He suggests that the analogy of email could be useful when explaining how Bitcoin works as a way to move valuable information quickly and securely.
- The author highlights the importance of frictionless and cheap transactions in order for Bitcoin to compete effectively with traditional payment methods.
- In Argentina, people are starting to use international transfer services like Taringa, which is integrating Bitcoin into its platform to facilitate faster and cheaper transfers.
- Popper believes that the Argentinian experiment could pave the way for broader adoption of Bitcoin by ordinary people.
- He also discusses the role of individuals within the Bitcoin ecosystem, emphasizing the importance of people who are passionate about technology and willing to influence others through storytelling and evangelism.


## a16z Podcast | Why SaaS Revenue is Worth More Than Traditional Software Sales

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XXJpk14PQkA](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XXJpk14PQkA)

- SaaS (Software as a Service) business model
    - Recurring revenue, high retention, and low churn
    - Cohort analysis to understand customer lifetime value
    - High valuation due to inherent profitability and cash flow generation
    - Transformation in the software industry from perpetual licenses to SaaS models
        - Mainframe to client-server transformation
        - Cloud computing as the next major shift
    - Metrics for understanding business performance:
        - Lifetime Value of a Customer (LTV) compared to Cost of Acquiring a Customer (CAC)
        - Regression analysis to identify key drivers of growth and retention
    - Internal metrics for managing the business:
        - Segment analysis to understand different customer segments and their needs
        - Understanding the impact of deferred revenue on financial statements
    - External metrics used by public companies:
        - Calculated Billings as a proxy for revenue growth
        - Lack of standardization in SaaS metrics across industries and companies
- Managing the transition from perpetual licenses to SaaS models:
    - Engineering challenges in rebuilding products for a multitenant architecture
    - Business challenges in transitioning sales, marketing, and customer support teams
    - Incentivizing sales representatives to focus on new business acquisition rather than renewals or upsells
- Compensation structures for SaaS businesses:
    - Commissionable amounts based on annual contract values (ACV)
    - Quotas set for new business reps to ensure consistent revenue growth
- Advice for portfolio companies considering going public:
    - Stay private as long as possible due to access to capital and the ability to focus on long-term growth without dealing with short-term market pressures.


## a16z Podcast | Good Bubbles, Bad Bubbles -- and Where Unicorns Come from

- He argues that the current environment for IPOs is challenging due to low interest rates, liquidity, and competition from public market investors.
- Janeway highlights the importance of building a self-sustaining cash flow operation as a key metric for startup success.
- He also emphasizes the need for venture capitalists to hedge against uncertainty by maintaining enough cash reserves and strategic influence in their investments.
- The concept of "unicorn" companies, which are privately held startups with high valuations, is discussed, with Janeway suggesting that these firms may be overvalued due to market hype and limited access to public markets.
- He also points out that many successful startup founders have experience surviving failed ventures or working at large corporations before launching their own businesses.
- Janeway believes that the role of venture capitalists in funding research and development has evolved over time, with a greater focus on commercializing technology rather than purely scientific research.
- He also notes that some industries, such as biotech, have seen significant consolidation among large companies acquiring early-stage startups to gain access to new technologies or products.
- Finally, Janeway discusses the importance of trial and error in building successful businesses, arguing that this approach allows entrepreneurs to learn from their mistakes and adapt quickly to changing market conditions.

## a16z Podcast | Making Security More Useable

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xesaUK2Mfzk](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xesaUK2Mfzk)

- Tom MacKinnon, CEO of Octa, discusses security strategies with Michael Copeland.
- Security is constantly evolving and the perimeter is always changing.
- Attackers are motivated, well-funded, and collaborative.
- The key to security is understanding that it's a constant battle and that there will be breaches.
- Security professionals need to focus on usability and making security more accessible for end users.
- Training and education at the grassroots level are essential for building a strong security culture within an organization.
- Designing with usability in mind is crucial when creating secure systems.
- The importance of performance, scalability, and security cannot be overstated when developing large-scale systems.
- Voice recognition technology can be used to improve the security of call centers by adding a layer of authentication.
- The use of biometric authentication methods like fingerprint readers is becoming more popular as they offer an easy way for users to secure their devices.
- The rise of Internet of Things (IoT) devices presents new challenges and opportunities for security professionals.
- Security must be built into every aspect of an organization, from network authentication to hardware monitoring.
- Least privilege access is a critical concept in security, as it ensures that only necessary privileges are granted to users.
- Monitoring systems can help organizations detect and respond to breaches more quickly.
- The importance of having a clear understanding of what needs to be protected cannot be overstated.
- Security must be flexible enough to adapt to changing technologies and threats.
- Regulation plays an important role in shaping security strategies, especially for international companies.


## a16z Podcast | Barbarians at the Gate -- How to Think About Enterprise Security Today

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6f7urZ4TtRc](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6f7urZ4TtRc)

- Introduction by Michael Copeland
- Andrew Rubin, CEO of Loomio, and Andrew Gough, Banga, CEO and co-founder of Bromium, discuss the changing landscape of security in a digital world.
- The panelists agree that as more aspects of life become digitized, the need for robust security measures becomes increasingly important.
- Rubin highlights the shift from thinking about security as a binary state (safe or breached) to considering it as an ongoing process that requires constant adaptation and improvement.
- Banga emphasizes the importance of understanding the evolving nature of threats and how they are changing in response to new technologies like cloud computing, mobile devices, and consumerization.
- The panelists discuss the challenges faced by enterprises when trying to balance speed and agility with security concerns, particularly as more companies move their operations into the cloud.
- They also touch on the growing trend of customer-centric design in security solutions, where users are given more control over how their data is protected and managed.
- Banga talks about the concept of "microsegmentation," which involves breaking down large networks into smaller, more manageable pieces that can be more easily secured and monitored.
- The panelists also discuss the potential benefits of adopting a more offensive approach to cybersecurity, where organizations actively work to prevent attacks rather than simply reacting to them after they have occurred.
- They acknowledge that this shift in mindset requires a significant amount of courage and willingness to take risks, especially given the rapidly changing nature of the threat landscape.
- The panelists conclude by reiterating the importance of staying informed about new developments in security technology and being prepared to adapt one's strategies accordingly.

## a16z Podcast | The Five Stages of Bitcoin -- Disdain, Dismissal, Curiosity, Oh F**k!, and Acceptance

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=p7aA4eknz7U](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=p7aA4eknz7U)

- Five stages of Bitcoin acceptance
  - Skepticism/Dismissal: Initial disbelief and dismissal of Bitcoin as a scam or fad.
  - Curiosity: Gradual curiosity piqued by growing attention and interest.
  - Aha Moment: Realization that Bitcoin is a groundbreaking innovation with real-world applications.
  - Acceptance: Recognition of the potential of Bitcoin to disrupt traditional financial systems and create new opportunities.
  - Advocacy: Active promotion and support for the adoption and growth of Bitcoin as a viable alternative to traditional currencies.
- Key Players in Wall Street's Crypto Journey
  - New York Stock Exchange (NYSE)
  - Andreessen Horowitz (a16z)
  - USAA
  - BBVA
  - Noble Markets
  - JP Morgan Chase & Co.
- Trust and Bitcoin: The Role of Blockchain Technology
  - Trust in traditional financial systems is built on intermediaries like banks, which verify transactions and maintain records of ownership.
  - Bitcoin's blockchain technology eliminates the need for intermediaries by creating a decentralized system where transactions are verified and recorded by miners.
  - This allows for peer-to-peer exchange without the need for trust in a third party, but it also requires users to trust the integrity of the blockchain and its miners.
- The Future of Bitcoin: Challenges and Opportunities
  - One of the biggest challenges facing Bitcoin is building trust among users and institutions. This requires educating people about how the technology works and demonstrating its reliability and security.
  - Another challenge is addressing concerns around money laundering, hacking, and other criminal activities associated with cryptocurrencies.
  - Despite these challenges, there are also significant opportunities for growth and innovation in the Bitcoin ecosystem, particularly as more institutions and individuals begin to recognize its potential benefits.
- The Role of Unbanked Populations in Cryptocurrency Adoption
  - Many unbanked populations around the world could benefit from cryptocurrencies like Bitcoin because they provide a way to send money without relying on traditional banking systems or intermediaries.
  - There is growing interest in exploring how cryptocurrencies can be used to address financial inclusion and empower individuals who have been excluded from traditional financial systems.
- The Future of Cryptocurrency Regulation
  - As more institutions and individuals begin to adopt cryptocurrencies, there will likely be increased pressure for governments and regulatory bodies to develop clear guidelines and standards for their use.
  - This could involve creating new laws or regulations that govern the issuance, exchange, and storage of cryptocurrencies, as well as addressing concerns around money laundering, tax evasion, and other potential risks associated with their use.


## a16z Podcast | Government, Startups, & Innovation -- with U.S. Secretary of Defense Ash Carter

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eYzb-s4ToKs](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eYzb-s4ToKs)

- US Secretary of Defense Ash Carter discusses the importance of partnership between Silicon Valley and the Department of Defense.
- He mentions that GPS technology is expensive to launch, operate, and maintain but is essential for military operations.
- Carter suggests that a MEMS chip could replace the need for satellites in some cases, making it more cost-effective and less vulnerable to jamming.
- He also discusses the evolution of commercial-driven innovation and how the Department of Defense plays a role in this ecosystem.
- The Secretary highlights the need for lower barriers to entry for startups and the importance of an open pathway for success without being acquired by large companies.
- Carter talks about creating an innovation unit within the Department of Defense that will work with venture capital firms, market players, and technology developers.
- He emphasizes the need for matching approaches between bright people and the marketplace, as well as connecting innovators to users and developers.
- The Secretary also addresses security concerns, especially in light of recent cyber attacks and hacking incidents.
- He mentions that there is a growing industry around cybersecurity but acknowledges that it is still an area where investment needs to be increased.
- Carter highlights two principal roles for the Department of Defense in the security domain: threat sharing information and interactive defense, which involves actively monitoring both external and internal threats.


## a16z Podcast | How One Startup Went from Being Banned by Regulators to Being Open for Business

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AfF4suZWYVM](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AfF4suZWYVM)

- Zenefits, a startup that helps companies manage HR, faced regulatory issues in Utah.
- The company's business model involved giving away its core system for free and making money through various services.
- Utah's insurance commissioner took action against Zenefits, claiming it had an unfair advantage over competitors.
- This led to a public outcry from consumers and tech community members who supported Zenefits.
- A state representative introduced a bill that clarified the law and protected Zenefits from being banned.
- The startup successfully lobbied for support from key politicians, including the governor and lieutenant governor.
- Utah's tech community played an important role in rallying support for Zenefits.
- Startups facing similar issues should focus on identifying their constituencies (e.g., clients, small business owners, conservative political organizations) and building relationships with influential individuals within these groups.

## a16z Podcast | Messaging is the Medium

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AzLaF2kPY4Y](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AzLaF2kPY4Y)

- Facebook's smartphone social platform:
  - Factors that have contributed to the emergence of this platform:
    + Smartphones and social platforms are now inseparable.
    + The app has direct access to a user’s address book, photo library, camera, location, push notification, etc.
    + Users can easily share photos on their new social apps without uploading them first.
  - Implications:
    + App developers have to compete with the built-in smartphone features and services.
    + The app has to be incredibly easy to install, use, and share for it to succeed in this market.
    + Users can easily switch between different social apps without much hassle.
  - Future trends:
    + Social messaging apps are becoming increasingly popular.
    + There is a new type of using media platforms that involve seeing something happen on one platform, telling friends who already use it, and not having to check another site or app.
    + The use of chat-based interfaces for social networking is growing rapidly.
    - Facebook's second wave: 
      - In the last two years, Facebook has been focusing on building platforms that can accommodate various types of content and services.
        + This includes things like messaging apps, video sharing platforms, etc.
        + The success of Instagram and WhatsApp shows that this strategy is working well for them.
          + They have also acquired other companies to help them expand their reach even further.
      - One interesting finding is how people use different types of social media platforms:
        + Some people prefer using desktop web browsers while others prefer using mobile devices.
          + However, no matter which platform they choose, the most important thing is getting people to install the app.
  - Facebook's acquisition strategy:
    - By acquiring other companies, Facebook can quickly expand its user base and offer new features to its existing users.
      + This has been very successful for them in the past few years.
      - However, it also means that they need to constantly keep up with the latest trends and technologies in order to stay ahead of their competitors.
  - The future of social media platforms:
    - As more people switch from desktop computers to mobile devices, social media companies will have to adapt accordingly.
      + This means creating apps that are easy to use and install on smartphones and tablets.
      + It also means finding new ways to engage users and keep them coming back for more.
        + One possible solution is by using chat-based interfaces, which allow users to interact with each other without having to leave the app.
  - The role of notifications in social media platforms:
    - Notifications play a crucial role in keeping users engaged with their favorite apps and services.
      + By sending timely updates and reminders, companies can encourage users to come back and use their products more often.
        + However, this also means that they need to be careful not to overwhelm their users with too many messages or alerts.
  - The impact of Apple's and Google's strategies on Facebook:
    - Both Apple and Google have been trying to create their own ecosystems for mobile devices, which could potentially threaten Facebook's dominance in the market.
      + However, it also gives them an opportunity to collaborate with these companies and offer new features and services to their users.
        + For example, Apple recently introduced a new feature called "Apple Pay," which allows users to make purchases directly within certain apps using their fingerprints or facial recognition technology.


## a16z Podcast | How to Lead, Not Manage Your Board

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aTSFMTWQzKU](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aTSFMTWQzKU)

- Importance of building a board
    - VCs and CEOs should consider adding domain experts early in the company's life
    - Board members with experience scaling companies can provide valuable guidance
    
- Board meeting best practices
    - Board meetings should have an agenda that is set ahead of time
    - Meetings should be concise, clear, and compelling
    - Encourage active participation and open discussion among board members
    - Regularly review and update the board composition to ensure it remains relevant and effective
    
- Role of a CEO in building a board
    - The CEO should take an active role in selecting and onboarding new board members
    - A good CEO will be able to navigate the balance between having a diverse board and ensuring that there is cohesion among its members
    - The CEO should also be prepared to communicate regularly with their board, both during meetings and outside of them
    
- Frequency of board meetings
    - Board meeting frequency can vary depending on the stage of the company
    - Early-stage companies may have more frequent meetings as they need guidance and direction from their board
    - Later-stage companies may have less frequent meetings as they become more self-sufficient
    
- The importance of preparation for board meetings
    - Both the CEO and the board members should prepare thoroughly for each meeting
    - This includes reviewing relevant materials, gathering data, and thinking through key issues that need to be discussed
    
- Board member expectations
    - Board members should be expected to provide strategic guidance and advice to the company
    - They should also be willing to roll up their sleeves and help out when needed
   
- The role of a board in helping a company grow
    - A good board can provide valuable insights and guidance that can help a company grow and scale effectively
    - They can also act as a sounding board for the CEO and other executives, helping them to make informed decisions about the future direction of the company

  - The issue of who is held accountable in the event of a data breach is becoming increasingly important, as more companies are being sued by shareholders for not having adequate security measures in place.
  - There is a growing relationship between government and Silicon Valley, but it is often fraught with tension and mistrust. The Snowden leaks have only exacerbated this situation, making it difficult for both sides to work together on important issues.
  - Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies are gaining popularity as a way to securely transfer value online. However, there are still many challenges that need to be addressed before they can become widely adopted.
  - The Internet of Things (IoT) is becoming increasingly popular, but it also presents new security risks that need to be addressed. As more and more devices become connected to the internet, the potential for hacking and data breaches increases.
  - The tech industry has grown rapidly in recent years, and it is now starting to have a significant impact on the global economy. As more people gain access to technology, there will likely be an increase in economic growth and innovation. However, this also means that there will be more disruption and change in the way businesses operate.

## a16z Podcast | Public or Private? Finding the Right Board Seat

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pvH5eilmfwY](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pvH5eilmfwY)

- 16z Podcast Interview with Board Members
    - Private vs Public Boards:
        - Private boards are often smaller and more focused on helping the CEO scale the company. They're usually less structured than public boards, which already have a solid governance structure in place.
    - Ambition for Joining Boards:
        - Board service can provide valuable learning experiences, networking opportunities, and exposure to different industries and leaders. It also allows individuals to give back and contribute their skills and experience to help another company grow.
    - Differences Between Public & Private Company Board Roles:
        - In a public company board role, there's often more focus on compliance, governance, and long-term strategy. In contrast, private companies may be more focused on helping the CEO scale the business or addressing specific challenges that arise during growth.
    - Importance of Networking for Board Service:
        - Building relationships with other board members, CEOs, and industry leaders can help individuals find potential board opportunities and demonstrate their value as a director.
    - Skills & Experience Needed to Succeed on Boards:
        - Successful board members often have a combination of functional expertise, business experience, and strong communication skills. They're also able to contribute in various ways beyond their area of expertise, such as providing strategic guidance or helping the company navigate complex issues.
    - Balancing Board Service with Other Responsibilities:
        - Balancing board service with a full-time job can be challenging, but it's important for individuals to manage their time effectively and prioritize their commitments accordingly. This may involve setting clear expectations with their employer or finding ways to streamline their workload.
    - Advice for First-Time Board Members:
        - New board members should take the time to learn about the company, its industry, and its competitors before attending their first meeting. They should also be prepared to ask questions, listen carefully, and contribute valuable insights based on their own experience and expertise.
    - Key Challenges & Opportunities in Seattle's Tech Scene:
        - The Seattle tech scene is growing rapidly, thanks in part to the presence of prominent companies like Amazon and Microsoft. However, it also faces challenges such as attracting top talent from other regions and maintaining a competitive edge in an increasingly crowded market.

  * The need for better battery life and more efficient use of space
  * The potential for a secondary screen on the wrist
  * The importance of preserving information overload and filtering unnecessary notifications
  * The possibility of smartwatches becoming fashion accessories rather than just functional devices
* Discussion about the value of technology products
  * Apple is creating an "object desire" with its products by focusing on user experience, design, and utility
  * The iPhone and iPad are examples of this strategy
  * The potential for future products to follow a similar approach
  * The idea that technology should be in the background, enabling experiences rather than being the focus of attention
* Discussion about the future of smartphones and other devices
  * The possibility of a future where devices like smartwatches are more important than smartphones
    + The potential for devices to become "lifestyle objects" that people can spend money on simply because they find them pleasing or enjoyable
    + The idea that people will be willing to pay more for these types of products if they offer a better user experience and are more aesthetically pleasing than traditional devices.
* Conclusion
  * The gold watch is an interesting addition to Apple's product line, but its impact on the overall market remains to be seen.
  * The potential for smartwatches to become more popular as people spend more time using their phones and other devices.
  * The importance of creating products that offer a better user experience and are more aesthetically pleasing than traditional devices.


## a16z Podcast | Embracing Sales

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iJQ5P1_bGLE](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iJQ5P1_bGLE)

    - Introduction to podcast and conference
        - Michael Copeland, Chris Wanstrath (GitHub co-founder), Peter Levine (Andreessen Horowitz board member) are the panelists.
    - Sale of GitHub organization
        - The sale of GitHub as an organization was not initially planned. It was a result of building a strong sales team and understanding customer needs.
    - Building a Sales Team
        - Initially, there was reluctance to build a sales team due to concerns over company culture. However, the need for a sales team became apparent when customers started asking how they could use GitHub internally within their organizations.
        - The sales team enabled developers to promote the product internally and voice their opinions within the organization.
    - Importance of Sales in Technology Companies
        - Sales is an essential part of any technology company, as it allows for increased revenue per customer. It also helps to build relationships with customers and understand their needs better.
        - Sales teams can help to educate customers about the product and its benefits, as well as provide support and assistance when needed.
    - Building a Successful Sales Organization at GitHub
        - The sales organization at GitHub was built by hiring people who shared the company's values and beliefs. This helped to create a unified culture within the organization.
        - The use of internal communication tools, such as chat and email, allowed for better collaboration between different departments within the company.
    - Integrating Sales and Engineering Teams
        - It is essential to have open communication between the sales and engineering teams within a technology company. This can be achieved by having regular meetings and using internal communication tools.
        - The sales team at GitHub used GitHub's own platform to communicate with engineers and developers, which helped to create a sense of unity within the organization.
    - Handling Feedback from Customers
        - Customer feedback is crucial for any technology company, as it helps to improve the product and meet customer needs better. The sales team at GitHub used customer feedback to make decisions about product changes and improvements.
    - Future Growth of Sales Teams in Technology Companies
        - As technology companies grow, they will need to expand their sales teams to keep up with demand. This will require hiring new people who share the company's values and beliefs.
        - It is essential to have a unified culture within the organization, as this will help to create a sense of unity and purpose among employees.
    - Conclusion
        - The panelists discussed the importance of sales in technology companies and how it can help to improve customer relationships and increase revenue per customer. They also talked about the challenges of building a successful sales organization within a technology company and how it can be done effectively.

## a16z Podcast | Tools for How We Work Today

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=njTZhneHoCQ](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=njTZhneHoCQ)

- Slack was founded in 2013 by Stewart Butterfield, who previously built a multiplayer game and experienced issues with communication within his team.
- The original goal of Slack was to build a web-based, massively multiplayer game, but it evolved into a collaboration software focused on improving internal communications within companies.
- Early use cases for Slack involved the founders using IRC (Internet Relay Chat) and noticing its shortcomings compared to a more modern communication tool.
- One of the key features of Slack is its search functionality, which allows users to easily find messages and files within the platform.
- The mobile version of Slack was developed early on, as the founders recognized the importance of catering to a workforce that was increasingly using mobile devices.
- Slack's pricing model is designed to encourage organizations to adopt the tool across their entire team, rather than just a few individuals.
- One of the key challenges faced by Slack has been integrating with other tools and platforms within an organization's tech stack, as well as managing the vast amount of data that flows through the platform.
- Another challenge faced by Slack is balancing the need for security and privacy while still providing a user-friendly experience.
- One of the key strengths of Slack is its ability to integrate with other tools and platforms, which allows users to streamline their workflow and increase productivity.
- The future of Slack may involve further integrations with other tools and platforms, as well as continued improvements in search functionality and mobile capabilities.

  - They also discuss the challenges of designing products that can be easily integrated into existing workflows and systems.
- The Future of IOT & Key Takeaways
  - Benedict Evans believes that 2015 will be an interesting year for IOT, with both incumbent companies and startups making significant strides in developing new products and services.
  - He also emphasizes the importance of building technology that is open, scalable, and able to work across different platforms and devices.


## a16z Podcast | Dumb Storage Gets Smart

- Peter Levine, General Partner at Andreessen Horowitz, interviews Paula Long, CEO and founder of Data Gravity.
- Paula Long co-founded EqualLogic, which was acquired by Dell for $1.4 billion in 2008.
- Data Gravity is a storage company that aims to make data intelligent by providing insights and value from within the storage layer itself.
- Peter Levine talks about the evolution of storage technology over time and how it has become more intelligent and automated.
- The concept of "data gravity" refers to the idea that data attracts applications and services due to its inherent value and importance.
- Data Gravity's approach is centered around providing intelligence at the storage array level, which allows for better management, optimization, and security of unstructured data.
- Paula Long believes that traditional storage companies will struggle to survive in the future as the market shifts towards more intelligent, software-defined solutions.
- Peter Levine discusses the potential impact of "data gravity" on the broader storage industry and how it could lead to new innovations and opportunities for companies like Data Gravity.
- Paula Long emphasizes the importance of understanding data privacy and compliance issues when dealing with unstructured data, especially in large organizations and government entities.
- The conversation also touches upon the growing trend of "Internet of Things" (IoT) devices generating massive amounts of data, which will require more intelligent storage solutions to handle effectively.
- Peter Levine suggests that the future of storage will involve a combination of hardware and software components working together seamlessly to provide better performance, scalability, and security for users.
- Paula Long believes that companies like Data Gravity will play an important role in shaping the future of data centers by providing innovative solutions that can help organizations manage their data more effectively.


## a16z Podcast | Why the Datacenter Needs an Operating System

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mpFp7AH6arE](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mpFp7AH6arE)

- Benjamin Hyneman, former Microsoft engineer and current CEO of Mesosphere, discusses the concept of a Data Center Operating System (DCOS)
- DCOS is designed to manage resources efficiently in large data centers
- Traditional operating systems allocate CPU, memory, disk, and network resources on a single computer. In contrast, DCOS manages these resources across multiple machines or servers within a data center
- The goal of DCOS is to maximize resource utilization by dynamically allocating and reallocating resources as needed
- DCOS provides an interface for developers to launch tasks and manage applications running on the data center infrastructure
- DCOS can be used to run distributed systems, such as Apache Kafka, Apache Spark, Cassandra, and Hadoop
- The advantage of using DCOS is that it allows organizations to build and deploy applications more quickly and efficiently than traditional operating systems
- Some companies that are already using DCOS include Twitter, Airbnb, HubSpot, eBay, and PayPal
- In the future, Benjamin Hyneman believes that DCOS will become increasingly important as more organizations move their infrastructure to the cloud

## a16z Podcast | Gateway Gadgets to the Internet of Things

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Me0GUI1PT34](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Me0GUI1PT34)

- General Partner of Andreessen Horowitz, Scott Weis, discusses connected home internet things at a conference.
- The preponderance of sensors and cheap battery and processor technology is driving the growth of connected home products.
- The challenge in this space is creating a platform that can unify disparate apps and devices.
- There are two main categories of connected home products: security and lighting.
- Security products might include home automation systems like thermostats, while lighting could involve smart bulbs or light switches.
- The future of the connected home will likely involve more sophisticated "recipes" that can automate tasks based on user preferences and behaviors.
- Some potential use cases for these recipes could include setting a recipe to turn off all lights when someone goes to sleep, or ensuring that the garage door is closed before leaving the house.
- There are concerns about unintended consequences of these technologies, such as privacy issues or unexpected energy usage.
- California has implemented new laws requiring offices built after 2015 to include light sensors and motion detectors in every room used for lighting.
- The wink hub is an example of a platform that can connect multiple devices together within the home.
- There are also emerging products that aim to automate household chores, such as laundry folding robots or smart kitchen appliances.
- Biometric authentication technologies like fingerprint scanners could play a role in securing access to homes in the future.
- The lock industry may be disrupted by new technologies that allow users to unlock doors using their smartphones or other devices.
- Other potential transformative retail technologies include keyless hotel rooms and self-checkout kiosks at airports.

## a16z Podcast | Ecommerce and the Holiday Shopping Collision

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bsdjLaDvEu0](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bsdjLaDvEu0)

- Jeff Jordan, General Partner at Andreessen Horizontec, discusses the challenges and opportunities in ecommerce.
- The expectation of fast shipping during holidays has led to a "collision" between logistics companies and online retailers.
- Amazon sets the bar high for customer service, free delivery, and quick returns.
- Ecommerce companies need to differentiate themselves through value propositions such as flash sales or personalized subscription boxes.
- The holiday shopping season is crucial for physical retailers, but many are struggling due to fixed costs and competition from ecommerce.
- Mall-based retailers are embracing omnichannel strategies to compete with online retailers.
- Online grocery and personal care categories have seen significant growth in recent years.
- Teen apparel brands like Abercrombie & Fitch, American Eagle, and Aeropostale are struggling due to the shift to online shopping.
- Starbucks has experienced a decline in foot traffic at their stores as more people shop online.
- Amazon's scale advantage makes it difficult for other ecommerce companies to compete directly with them.
- UPS and USPS are facing challenges in keeping up with the growth of ecommerce, especially during peak seasons like holidays.
- Drone delivery may be an interesting use case for Amazon, but it is not likely to become widespread anytime soon.
- Payment methods like Apple Pay are changing the way people shop both online and offline.


## a16z Podcast | Where's My Stuff? -- The Lowdown on Logistics and Ops

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Do53igvc9JI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Do53igvc9JI)

- Importance of operation in ecommerce
  - Operation is the backbone of any business, especially in the ecommerce industry.
  - It involves managing logistics, inventory, customer service, and more.
- Challenges faced by operations in ecommerce
  - Scaling up: As businesses grow, operations need to scale up accordingly. This can be challenging as it requires hiring new people, expanding facilities, and adjusting processes.
  - Customization: Ecommerce customers often want personalized products or services. Operations need to be able to handle this while still maintaining efficiency and cost-effectiveness.
  - Supply chain management: Ensuring that products are available when customers want them can be difficult, especially if there are supply chain issues or delays.
  - Customer service: Providing excellent customer service is crucial in ecommerce. Operations need to be able to handle customer inquiries and complaints quickly and efficiently.
- Metrics used by operations in ecommerce
  - Cost control: Monitoring costs and finding ways to reduce them is important for any operation.
  - Quality: Ensuring that products are of high quality and meet customer expectations is essential.
  - Delivery time: Getting products to customers quickly and efficiently is crucial in ecommerce.
- Importance of culture and attitude in operations
  - A positive culture and attitude can help employees work together more effectively and solve problems quickly.
  - Negative attitudes or poor behavior can lead to mistakes, defects, and other issues.
- The role of technology in operations
  - Technology can help automate processes, improve efficiency, and provide better customer service.
  - However, it also requires investment and ongoing maintenance.
- Importance of security and privacy in ecommerce
  - Protecting customer data and ensuring that transactions are secure is crucial in ecommerce.
  - This requires careful planning and implementation of security measures.


## a16z Podcast | The Next Phase of 3D Printing

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TMMlLsrhxb4](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TMMlLsrhxb4)

- 3D Printing is a core manufacturing technology that leverages digital additive processes to build objects layer by layer.
- The software eating the world phenomenon impacts 3D printing, with rapid prototyping being a key area of focus in the industry.
- 3D printing enables the creation of complex and unique designs that are difficult or impossible to manufacture using traditional techniques.
- Designers play a crucial role in the 3D printing process, as they create digital models that are then printed into physical objects.
- The 3D printing landscape is rapidly evolving, with advancements in materials, software, and hardware driving innovation in the industry.
- There is a growing trend towards mass customization and personalization in the 3D printing market, as consumers seek to create unique and tailored products.
- The rise of 3D printing has disrupted traditional manufacturing processes, with companies now able to rapidly iterate and test product designs before bringing them to market.
- The 3D printing ecosystem encompasses a range of stakeholders, including material manufacturers, printer manufacturers, software developers, and designers.
- 3D printing is enabling new business models in the industry, such as on-demand manufacturing and online marketplaces for printed products.
- The growing popularity of 3D printing is driving innovation in industries beyond traditional manufacturing, such as healthcare and aerospace.
- As the technology continues to evolve, there is potential for further disruption in traditional manufacturing processes, with companies increasingly turning to 3D printing for rapid prototyping and on-demand production.


## a16z Podcast | The End of Ownership

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xEe2P4hjnRM](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xEe2P4hjnRM)

    - Joe Gebbia (Airbnb): 
        - Access is more important than ownership in today's digital age.
        - Music industry serves as an analogy for the shift towards access over ownership.
        - Airbnb empowers people to share their homes with others, creating a sense of community and trust.
    - Ben Uretsky (DigitalOcean): 
        - Cloud infrastructure enables businesses to scale quickly and efficiently without needing physical assets like servers.
        - DigitalOcean abstracts the concept of server space, presenting it as a variable cost resource called "droplets."
        - The cloud industry is leading the way in changing user behavior by providing flexible, on-demand services.
    - John Stanfield (LocalMotion): 
        - LocalMotion focuses on reducing fixed costs associated with owning large vehicle fleets.
        - By sharing vehicles among multiple users, companies can save money and optimize fleet usage.
        - The goal is to create a more efficient transportation system that benefits both businesses and consumers.
- Discussion Topics: 
    - How technology is changing the way we think about ownership and access.
    - The impact of sharing economy on traditional industries like hospitality, transportation, and real estate.
    - The role of data and analytics in driving innovation within the sharing economy.
    - The challenges faced by companies trying to adapt to a shared economy model.
- Summary: 
    - The panel discussed how technology is transforming our understanding of ownership and access, particularly within the sharing economy. They highlighted examples from industries such as hospitality (Airbnb), transportation (LocalMotion), and cloud computing (DigitalOcean). Each speaker emphasized the importance of flexibility, data-driven decision making, and building trust with customers in order to succeed in a shared economy environment.

## a16z Podcast | The (Definite) Optimism of Peter Thiel

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qhY5IlvxbE0](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qhY5IlvxbE0)

- Peter Thiel's early life: Born in Frankfurt, Germany; moved to the US at 13; grew up in California.
- PayPal founding story: Started as X.com, rebranded as Confinity with Elon Musk and Max Levchin; acquired by eBay for $1.5 billion in 2002.
- PayPal's early challenges: High burn rate, market volatility, and competition from other payment companies.
- Peter Thiel's entrepreneurial experience: Founded multiple successful companies including PayPal, Palantir Technologies, and Founders Fund.
- View on innovation: Believes in building monopolies to drive innovation and profitability.
- Perspective on Silicon Valley: Criticizes lack of competition and overemphasis on social impact.
- Thoughts on the 2000 dotcom bubble: Believes it was a result of government intervention and easy money policies.
- View on the current tech industry: Warns against another bubble driven by government bond purchasing and low interest rates.
- Monopoly versus commodity debate: Argues that monopolies are more innovative and profitable than commodities, but also highlights potential risks such as stagnation or misuse of power.
- Thiel's advice for entrepreneurs: Encourages founders to aim for monopolies and maintain control over their companies throughout their careers.

## a16z Podcast | Reinventing Media

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KkKt3prMdco](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KkKt3prMdco)

- Panelists: Margot van Mahas (Partner, 16z), Claire Kane Miller (New York Times), Alexis Madrigal (The Atlantic), Connie Guillermo (CNET)
- Key topics discussed: Medium as a platform for longform journalism, the changing landscape of news distribution, the role of analytics and data in storytelling, the impact of social media on journalism, the importance of understanding audience preferences, the rise of new online publications, the effect of technology on society and culture, the challenges faced by large tech companies, and the future of storytelling.
- Medium as a platform for longform journalism: Margot van Mahas highlights the reinvention of long-live publications like Medium, which have adapted to the changing landscape of news consumption. Claire Kane Miller discusses her role in helping launch upshot, a section within The New York Times that focuses on data-driven reporting and analysis.
- Changing landscape of news distribution: Panelists agree that technology has brought about significant changes in how news is distributed and consumed. Connie Guillermo talks about the evolution of CNET, which started as an entirely online publication and has since embraced new technologies like video and social media. Alexis Madrigal discusses the impact of platforms like Facebook and Twitter on news distribution and consumption, as well as the rise of analytics tools that help journalists understand how their stories are being shared and consumed.
- Role of analytics and data in storytelling: Panelists agree that data is playing an increasingly important role in journalism, helping reporters identify trends and patterns that can inform their reporting. However, they also acknowledge that there is a risk that data can overshadow the human element of storytelling.
- Impact of social media on journalism: Panelists discuss how platforms like Facebook and Twitter have changed the way journalists tell stories, as well as the challenges posed by these platforms in terms of maintaining journalistic integrity and reaching audiences. They also acknowledge that while social media has made it easier for journalists to share their work with a wider audience, it has also led to increased competition and pressure to produce content quickly.
- Importance of understanding audience preferences: Panelists emphasize the importance of understanding audience preferences when creating content, whether it's through analytics tools or other forms of feedback. They also discuss how this understanding can help journalists create more engaging and effective stories that resonate with their readers.
- Rise of new online publications: Panelists discuss the rise of new online publications like 538, Vox, and BuzzFeed, which have emerged in response to changing audience preferences and technology trends. They also acknowledge that these publications often take a different approach to journalism than traditional print publications, focusing on data-driven reporting and analysis rather than traditional news reporting.
- Effect of technology on society and culture: Panelists discuss how technology has changed the way we live our lives and interact with one another, as well as the impact of this change on various industries, including journalism. They also acknowledge that while technology has brought about many positive changes, it has also led to new challenges and concerns, such as privacy and data security.
- Challenges faced by large tech companies: Panelists discuss the challenges faced by large tech companies like Google, Facebook, and Apple, which have become increasingly influential in recent years. They acknowledge that these companies often struggle to balance their desire for growth and profitability with their commitment to user privacy and data security.
- Future of storytelling: Panelists discuss the future of storytelling in the age of technology and social media, as well as the challenges posed by this new landscape. They acknowledge that while technology has brought about many changes in how stories are told and consumed, it has also created new opportunities for journalists to experiment with different forms of storytelling and reach new audiences.

## a16z Podcast | Secrets, Power Laws, and Technology – The Ideas of “Zero to One”

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OVrF65dBYlU](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OVrF65dBYlU)

- "Zero to One" by Peter Thiel and Blake Masters
- Themes: Competition vs. Monopoly, Secret Startup Idea, Power Law, Globalization vs. Localization, Investment Context
- Secret Startup Idea: A powerful idea that creates a new market or transforms an existing one. It's not just about iterating on existing ideas.
- Power Law: The unequal distribution of wealth and value in the world. In the startup world, a few companies dominate while many others struggle to survive.
- Investment Context: Venture capitalists look for startups that have the potential to create a monopoly or dominance in their market. They use power law principles to identify these opportunities.
- Globalization vs. Localization: The book argues that globalization has led to commoditization, while localization creates opportunities for innovation and new markets.
- Competition vs. Monopoly: Startups should aim to create monopolies rather than competing with existing companies. This requires a unique value proposition that cannot be easily replicated.


## a16z Podcast | Apple Takes on Payments and Your Wrist

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sa3nU6nUbEA](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sa3nU6nUbEA)

- Benedict Evans from 16z discusses Apple's latest event
- iPhone 6 and 6 Plus unveiled with larger screens
- Higher end market wants bigger phones, willing to sacrifice ease of reach for more screen space
- Apple introduced a new feature called 'Reachability', which essentially moves the top half of the screen down when touched, allowing users to access the entire display with one hand
- The iPhone 6 and 6 Plus are both equipped with NFC (Near Field Communication) technology, which allows for contactless payments
- Apple Pay is the name of their new payment system, which works by securely storing your credit card information on your iPhone and allowing you to make purchases using just your fingerprint
- The process involves scanning a user's credit card with the iPhone's camera, then securely storing the card details in the device's 'Secure Element'
- Apple is partnering with Visa, MasterCard, and American Express for this initiative, as well as major banks like Citibank, Chase, and Bank of America
- The goal is to create a seamless user experience where users can simply hold their iPhone up to an NFC reader at a retail store, authenticate themselves using Touch ID, and complete their purchase without having to fumble around with physical credit cards or cash
- Apple's approach to payments is unique in that they are providing both the hardware (iPhone) and software (Apple Pay) needed for transactions, which could potentially give them a significant advantage over competitors like Google
- The success of Apple Pay will likely depend on the availability of NFC readers at retail locations, as well as widespread adoption among merchants and consumers alike
- Benedict also discusses the potential impact of virtualized credit cards on the future of payments, suggesting that it may become possible for users to obtain new credit card information directly from their iPhones in the near future
- He also touches upon the idea of creating a "club membership" around Apple products, where owning one device makes you more likely to purchase additional devices within the same ecosystem (e.g., iPhone -> iPad -> Apple Watch)
- Benedict believes that this strategy could help drive sales of accessories like smartwatches and fitness trackers, which are becoming increasingly popular among consumers

## a16z Podcast | Everything You Need to Know About Amazon

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fFbtZg9eQVw](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fFbtZg9eQVw)

## Summary of 16z Podcast with Benedict Evans: Amazon
- Amazon is a diverse company, not just an online retailer. It has separate business lines for physical mediums like books and DVDs.
- The company's revenue growth is accelerating, but it consistently reports zero profit. This is because Jeff Bezos aims to reinvest all profits back into the business.
- Amazon's operating cash flow margin has been relatively stable at around 6-8% over the past decade. However, its capital expenditure ratio has increased dramatically since 2010, leading to a significant increase in spending on warehouses and AWS infrastructure.
- Despite being unprofitable, Amazon is generating substantial economic returns through investments in high-growth businesses like AWS and new product categories.
- The company's long-term vision is evident in its willingness to invest heavily in future growth opportunities while maintaining a strong focus on innovation and customer satisfaction.
- Unlike other tech companies that prioritize short-term profitability, Amazon takes a longer-term approach by focusing on building infrastructure and platforms that can support long-term growth.
- The AWS platform is a prime example of this strategy, as it allows Amazon to expose internal systems to external customers while also generating significant revenue from its own use of the platform.
- The Prime subscription model further demonstrates Amazon's commitment to long-term growth by offering customers access to exclusive content and discounted shipping rates in exchange for an annual fee. This model helps to drive customer loyalty and increase sales volume, ultimately benefiting both Amazon and its suppliers.
- While some critics argue that Amazon's investments in video content may not be profitable, the company has demonstrated its ability to generate significant revenues from other areas of its business, such as selling headphones and offering discounted shipping rates.
- Ultimately, Jeff Bezos' vision for Amazon is one of continuous growth and innovation, with a focus on creating long-term value for shareholders and customers alike.

## a16z Podcast | Ben and Marc Explain (Practically) Everything – Part 1

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w54v-B2Sk1w](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w54v-B2Sk1w)

- 5 years since founding
- Thesis: Computer is a 75-year-old industry that has evolved from cracking codes during WW2 to making PCs accessible for rich people in Europe and the US. It's now entering an era where everyone will have smartphones, which are essentially computers for everyone.
- Software eats world: This refers to the idea that every industry is being disrupted by software. Marc Andreessen believes we're only at the beginning of this trend, with more industries yet to be transformed.
- The rise of smartphones and mobile devices is leading to a new era where everyone has access to the internet through their phones. This will change how businesses operate and interact with customers.

- The shift towards software-based solutions in industries like healthcare and education could lead to cost reductions and increased accessibility for everyone. This would require a significant shift in policy decisions and the creation of safety nets that enable people to transition into new roles without losing their livelihoods.
- The potential for artificial intelligence, drones, Bitcoin, virtual reality, and other technologies to transform industries is enormous. These technologies are still in their early stages but have already begun to disrupt traditional business models.
- Investing in software-based companies that are focused on solving complex problems is an important part of the firm's strategy. The goal is to identify companies that are building world-class products and services that can scale globally.
- The future of technology will be characterized by smaller devices with more powerful processors, which will allow for greater connectivity and data processing capabilities. This will lead to new innovations in areas like manufacturing, robotics, and transportation.
- The rise of smartphones is leading to a shift towards more experimental approaches to product development, as companies try to figure out what works best for their customers. This can sometimes lead to criticism from those who don't understand the process or think that everything should be perfect from the start.
- The firm believes that the future will be characterized by smart devices that are connected to the internet and able to respond to human needs. This will require a significant amount of experimentation and innovation, as well as collaboration between different industries and sectors.
- The firm is committed to supporting entrepreneurs who are building innovative companies in areas like venture capital, social networking, and real entrepreneurial communities. They believe that these types of companies are the future of technology and will help drive growth in the global economy.
- The rise of smartphones and mobile devices is leading to a more connected world where people can access information and services from anywhere at any time. This will continue to change how businesses operate and interact with customers, as well as how individuals consume content and engage with each other.
- The firm believes that the future of technology will be characterized by greater collaboration between different industries and sectors, as well as a focus on solving complex problems through software-based solutions. They also believe that the rise of smartphones and mobile devices will continue to drive innovation and growth in the global economy.


## a16z Podcast | The Topic That's Lasted the Entire History of Computing -- Bundling and Unbundling

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XWJ-xKT94t8](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XWJ-xKT94t8)

    - Andreessen Horowitz Podcast: Bundling and Unbundling in the Computing Industry
        - Hendricks Evans discussed the history of bundling and unbundling with Steven Sinofsky.
        - The topic has lasted throughout the entire history of computing.
        - The discussion revolved around the trend towards unbundling and feature-inside apps, which have become standalone applications.
        - Some examples include Facebook breaking into separate apps for different purposes, and Instagram separating from its parent company, Facebook.
        - The motivation behind this trend is limited screen real estate and changes in discovery dynamics.
        - Sinofsky mentioned that the history of computing can be seen as a story of innovation, and that both bundling and unbundling have their own merits.
   
    - China's App Market: A Different Approach to Bundling and Unbundling
        - The Chinese app market has taken a different approach to the traditional portal model, particularly on mobile devices.
        - Baidu, one of China's largest search engines, built an Maps app that includes booking options for restaurants, cinemas, hotels, and taxis within the same platform.
        - This approach allows users to find what they need without having to leave the app or search on Google.
   
    - The Evolution of Apps and Their Impact on User Behavior
        - As apps evolve, they are starting to monetize engagement and drive user engagement through features such as in-app purchases and subscription models.
        - In China, there is a strong focus on solving problems for users, which has led to the creation of many different aggregators that integrate various services into one platform.
   
    - The Future of Apps: A Balancing Act Between Discovery and Usability
        - As more apps are created, developers face the challenge of making their apps discoverable while also ensuring they are easy to use.
        - This balancing act requires developers to consider factors such as user flow, app integration, and how users interact with different services within an app.
   
    - The Importance of Single-Digit App Usage
        - According to a survey by The Wall Street Journal, people use an average of seven apps per day on their smartphones.
        - This number is significant because it helps developers understand which apps are most important to users and how they should prioritize their resources.
   
    - The Impact of Google and Apple on App Distribution
        - Both Google and Apple have a significant influence on app distribution, as they control the majority of the market for smartphone apps.
        - This influence can be seen in the way that both companies choose to highlight certain apps over others within their respective app stores.
   
    - The Importance of Discovery in the App Marketplace
        - As the number of apps continues to grow, developers must find new ways to make their apps discoverable to users.
        - This challenge is exacerbated by the fact that there are many different services and platforms available for users to choose from when looking for new apps to download.
   
    - The Importance of App Store Optimization (ASO)
        - ASO is becoming increasingly important as developers look for ways to make their apps more discoverable to users.
        - This involves optimizing the app's metadata, including its title, description, and keywords, in order to improve its visibility within app store search results.
   
    - The Importance of User Retention
        - In order to be successful, developers must focus on retaining their users once they have downloaded an app.
        - This can be achieved through various strategies such as offering personalized content, providing regular updates and improvements, and engaging with users through social media and other channels.
   
    - The Importance of App Analytics
        - App analytics play a crucial role in helping developers understand how their apps are performing and what changes they need to make in order to improve user engagement and retention.
        - By analyzing data such as user behavior, app usage patterns, and conversion rates, developers can gain valuable insights into how their apps are being used and what improvements they can make to enhance the overall user experience.


## a16z Podcast | The Consumerization of IT

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0pkZJaawMvI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0pkZJaawMvI)

- Peter Levine discusses the future of data centers and their evolution towards commodity hardware.
    - He believes that software will bridge the gap between unreliable hardware components, making them work better together.
    - Open source is seen as a major driving force in this transformation, with companies like Google and Facebook already using commodity off-the-shelf components to build their data center infrastructure.
    - The trend towards commoditization of hardware will lead to increased convergence between software components, with a focus on providing a single platform that can run multiple applications efficiently.
    - Legacy companies built around specific hardware boundaries may struggle to adapt to this new model, as they will need to rethink their entire business structure and cost structure.
- VMware is mentioned as an example of a company that has successfully adapted to this changing landscape by moving away from a Windows-centric approach and embracing Linux containers.
    - The use of containerization technology (such as Docker) allows for more efficient resource allocation and better isolation between different applications running on the same machine.
    - This trend towards open source solutions is seen as a viable business model, with companies like Red Hat making significant profits by providing support and customization services around open source software products.
- The importance of user interface design in next-generation data center companies is emphasized, particularly in the context of mobile devices and consumer software applications.

## a16z Podcast | Protecting Your Company from Itself: Why You Need HR

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WnaTTIfjoyI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WnaTTIfjoyI)

- HR in Startups: Shannon Callahan, a startup HR professional, talks about common mistakes companies make regarding HR.
  - Recruiters vs. HR: Companies often hire recruiters instead of HR professionals. However, this leads to a disconnect between recruiting and HR functions.
    * A world-class recruiter might be more focused on personality and salesmanship than understanding the nuances of HR.
    * An effective HR professional can help build a strong company culture and ensure that employees are aligned with the company's vision.
  - Hiring HR Professionals Early: Shannon emphasizes the importance of hiring an HR professional early in a startup's growth.
    * As companies grow, they need to address issues like employee diversity, onboarding, and performance management. An experienced HR person can help navigate these challenges.
  - Dress Codes & Company Culture: Shannon discusses how dress codes can impact company culture.
    * Startups often have a relaxed culture that may not align with traditional business attire. However, as companies grow, they need to consider how their culture will evolve and how it will be perceived by potential employees.
  - Onboarding & Employee Retention: Shannon highlights the importance of onboarding new employees effectively.
    * A well-designed onboarding process can help new hires feel welcomed and valued, which can improve employee retention rates.
  - Measuring Employee Performance: Shannon talks about how companies can measure employee performance.
    * Companies need to establish clear objectives for their employees and regularly evaluate their progress. This can help ensure that employees are productive and happy in their roles.
  - HR Metrics & Employee Engagement: Shannon discusses the importance of using HR metrics to track employee engagement and productivity.
    * By measuring key performance indicators, companies can better understand how their employees are performing and identify areas where they may need to improve.
- Key Takeaways:
  - Hiring an experienced HR professional early in a startup's growth can help address issues like employee diversity, onboarding, and performance management.
  - A well-designed onboarding process can help new hires feel welcomed and valued, which can improve employee retention rates.
  - Companies need to establish clear objectives for their employees and regularly evaluate their progress to ensure that they are productive and happy in their roles.
  - By measuring key performance indicators, companies can better understand how their employees are performing and identify areas where they may need to improve.


## a16z Podcast | When Large Scale Gets Really Massive -- Managing Today’s Enterprise Networks

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CxH3aQnVj24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CxH3aQnVj24)

- Tinium Orion is a real-time network monitoring and management platform that provides instant answers to complex queries across large networks.
- The platform uses a linear peer-to-peer networking architecture, which allows it to scale efficiently and provide real-time data without the need for centralized servers or databases.
- Tinium Orion enables users to ask questions in natural language and receive immediate, accurate responses, even when dealing with complex network environments and large numbers of devices.
- The platform also provides a powerful API that allows developers to build custom applications and integrations, as well as real-time monitoring and visualization tools for network data.

## a16z Podcast | The Two Big Problems With Thomas Piketty’s “Capital in the Twenty-First Century”

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ftbNWFy1WtI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ftbNWFy1WtI)

- Thomas Piketty's "Capital in the Twenty-First Century" discussed, criticized, and praised
- Piketty's diagnosis of growing inequality seen as powerful and reflective of increased intellectualism
- Concern over rising wealth concentration in top 1%
- Criticism of Piketty's economic theory: elasticity substitution and capital accumulation rates
- Issues with constant saving rate assumption in Piketty's argument
- Dynamic process of wealth accumulation highlighted, using Forbes 400 list as an example
- Discussion of entrepreneurial fortunes and their role in income inequality
- Importance of technology and globalization in reducing global inequality
- Consumption inequality decreasing due to microeconomic factors like deflation and technology advancements
- Power inequality declining with increasing representation from non-Western countries
- Emerging markets converging, leading to a more equal distribution of wealth within the United States
- Health disparities highlighted as a fundamental factor in income inequality
- Final thoughts on the importance of emerging markets and consumption experience equalization.


## a16z Podcast | Valuing Today's Fast-Growing Software Companies

URL: [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TQYtif-honA](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TQYtif-honA)

- SAS companies:
  - Evaluation based on revenue multiples and EPS.
  - Perpetual model vs traditional perpetual license.
  - Billings as a leading indicator of future cash flow and visibility.
  - Longer customer lifetime value and acquisition costs.
  - Sticky customers and decentralized purchasing decisions.
  - SAS companies have higher gross margins, allowing for more spending on sales, marketing, and R&D.
  - Multitenancy allows for cost sharing among multiple customers using the same infrastructure.
  - Economies of scale in R&D can lead to lower expenses over time.
  - The subscription-based business model differs from traditional perpetual license models, impacting financial statements and profitability.
